<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Lady Gaga</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p><b>Stefani Joanne Angelina Germanotta</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɛ/ short 'e' in 'bed'">ɛ</span><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span><span title="/iː/ long 'e' in 'seed'">iː</span></span> <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/dʒ/ 'j' in 'jam'">dʒ</span><span title="/ɜːr/ 'ur' in 'fur'">ɜːr</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span><span title="/ɒ/ short 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span> <span title="English pronunciation respelling"><a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i><b><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">STEF</span></span></b>-ə-nee</i></a></span> <span title="English pronunciation respelling"><a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i>jur-mə-<b><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">NOT</span></span></b>-ə</i></a></span>; born March 28, 1986), known professionally as <b>Lady Gaga</b>, is an American singer, songwriter and actress. She performed initially in theater, appearing in high school plays, and studied at <a href="/wiki/Collaborative_Arts_Project_21_(CAP21)" title="Collaborative Arts Project 21 (CAP21)">CAP21</a> through NYU's <a href="/wiki/Tisch_School_of_the_Arts" title="Tisch School of the Arts">Tisch School of the Arts</a> before dropping out to pursue a musical career. After leaving a rock band, participating in the <a href="/wiki/Lower_East_Side" title="Lower East Side">Lower East Side</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avant_garde" title="Avant garde">avant garde</a> performance art circuit, and being dropped from a contract with <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam Recordings</a>, Gaga worked as a songwriter for <a href="/wiki/Sony/ATV_Music_Publishing" title="Sony/ATV Music Publishing">Sony/ATV Music Publishing</a>. From there, <a href="/wiki/Akon" title="Akon">Akon</a> noticed her vocal abilities and helped her to sign a joint deal with <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a> and his own <a href="/wiki/KonLive_Distribution" title="KonLive Distribution">KonLive Distribution</a>.</p>
<p>Her debut album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fame" title="The Fame">The Fame</a></i> (2008) was a critical and commercial success that produced international chart-topping singles such as "<a href="/wiki/Just_Dance_(song)" title="Just Dance (song)">Just Dance</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Poker_Face_(Lady_Gaga_song)" title="Poker Face (Lady Gaga song)">Poker Face</a>". A follow-up EP, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fame_Monster" title="The Fame Monster">The Fame Monster</a></i> (2009), was met with a similar reception and "<a href="/wiki/Bad_Romance" title="Bad Romance">Bad Romance</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Telephone_(song)" title="Telephone (song)">Telephone</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Alejandro_(song)" title="Alejandro (song)">Alejandro</a>" were released, becoming successful singles. Her second full-length album <i><a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_(album)" title="Born This Way (album)">Born This Way</a></i> was released in 2011, topping the charts in more than 20 countries, including the United States, where it sold over one million copies in its first week. The album produced the number-one single "<a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_(song)" title="Born This Way (song)">Born This Way</a>". Her third album <i><a href="/wiki/Artpop" title="Artpop">Artpop</a></i>, released in 2013, topped the US charts and included the successful single "<a href="/wiki/Applause_(Lady_Gaga_song)" title="Applause (Lady Gaga song)">Applause</a>". In 2014, Gaga released a collaborative jazz album with <a href="/wiki/Tony_Bennett" title="Tony Bennett">Tony Bennett</a> titled <i><a href="/wiki/Cheek_to_Cheek_(album)" title="Cheek to Cheek (album)">Cheek to Cheek</a></i>, which became her third consecutive number one in the United States. For her work in the television series <i><a href="/wiki/American_Horror_Story:_Hotel" title="American Horror Story: Hotel">American Horror Story: Hotel</a></i>, Gaga won a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe Award</a> in 2016. She became the first woman to have four US number one albums in the 2010s when her fifth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Joanne_(album)" title="Joanne (album)">Joanne</a></i> (2016) topped the nation's charts.</p>
<p>With global album and single sales of 27 million and 146 million respectively, as of January 2016, she is one of the best-selling musicians of all time. Her achievements include twelve <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a>, three <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brit Awards</a>, and six <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a>. She is also the first artist to win the <a href="/wiki/Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame" title="Songwriters Hall of Fame">Songwriters Hall of Fame</a>'s Contemporary Icon Award. Other accolades include a Fashion Icon lifetime achievement award from the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Fashion_Designers_of_America" title="Council of Fashion Designers of America">Council of Fashion Designers of America</a> (2011), regular appearances on <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Artists of the Year lists and <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s power and earnings rankings. In 2013, Gaga finished second on <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s readers' poll of the most influential people of the past ten years, while in 2015, she was named <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Women_in_Music" title="Billboard Women in Music"><i>Billboard</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Woman of the Year</a>. She is known for her philanthropic work and social activism, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LGBT_rights" title="LGBT rights">LGBT rights</a> and her own non-profit organization, the <a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_Foundation" title="Born This Way Foundation">Born This Way Foundation</a>, which focuses on promoting youth empowerment and combating bullying.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_career">Life and career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1986.E2.80.932004:_Early_life">1986–2004: Early life</span></h3>
<p>Stefani Joanne Angelina Germanotta was born on March 28, 1986, at the <a href="/wiki/Lenox_Hill_Hospital" title="Lenox Hill Hospital">Lenox Hill Hospital</a> on <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Upper_East_Side" title="Upper East Side">Upper East Side</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> to a Catholic family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> She is the elder daughter of Cynthia Louise "Cindy" (Bissett) and Internet entrepreneur Joseph "Joe" Germanotta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tvguide_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-tvguide-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Gaga is of 75 percent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_American" title="Italian American">Italian</a> descent, and also has <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Canadian" title="French Canadian">French Canadian</a> ancestry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Gaga's sister Natali is a fashion student.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Despite her affluent upbringing on Manhattan's <a href="/wiki/Upper_West_Side" title="Upper West Side">Upper West Side</a>, she says that her parents "both came from lower-class families, so we've worked for everything—my mother worked eight to eight out of the house, in telecommunications, and so did my father."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jmgaga_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-jmgaga-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TimesOnlineDec09_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-TimesOnlineDec09-12">[12]</a></sup> From age eleven, she attended the <a href="/wiki/Convent_of_the_Sacred_Heart_(New_York_City)" title="Convent of the Sacred Heart (New York City)">Convent of the Sacred Heart</a>, a private, all-girls Roman Catholic school on Manhattan's Upper East Side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Times_Online.co.uk_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Times_Online.co.uk-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-independent-15">[15]</a></sup> She described her academic life in high school as "very dedicated, very studious, very disciplined" but also "a bit insecure". "I used to get made fun of for being either too provocative or too eccentric, so I started to tone it down. I didn't fit in, and I felt like a freak."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> In 2014, Gaga confessed to being raped at the age of 19. She stated, "I went through some horrific things that I'm able to laugh [at] now, because I've gone through a lot of mental and physical therapy and emotional therapy to heal over the years".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Gaga later said that she suffers from <a href="/wiki/Posttraumatic_stress_disorder" title="Posttraumatic stress disorder">posttraumatic stress disorder</a> because of the rape, and that support from doctors, family, and friends "really saved my life".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"It is a daily effort for me ... to regulate my nervous system so that I don’t panic over circumstances that to many would seem like normal life situations. Examples are leaving the house or being touched by strangers who simply want to share their enthusiasm for my music".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">—Gaga on her struggle with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PTSD" title="PTSD">PTSD</a></cite></div>
<p>Gaga began playing the piano at the age of four, wrote her first piano ballad at thirteen, and started to perform at <a href="/wiki/Open_mic" title="Open mic">open mic</a> nights by the age of fourteen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> She performed lead roles in high school productions, including Adelaide in <i><a href="/wiki/Guys_and_Dolls" title="Guys and Dolls">Guys and Dolls</a></i> and Philia in <i><a href="/wiki/A_Funny_Thing_Happened_on_the_Way_to_the_Forum" title="A Funny Thing Happened on the Way to the Forum">A Funny Thing Happened on the Way to the Forum</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-growingupgaga_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-growingupgaga-21">[21]</a></sup> She also appeared in a very small role as a mischievous classmate in the television drama series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sopranos" title="The Sopranos">The Sopranos</a></i> in a 2001 episode titled "<a href="/wiki/The_Telltale_Moozadell" title="The Telltale Moozadell">The Telltale Moozadell</a>". She auditioned for New York shows without success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jmgaga_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-jmgaga-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> She also studied <a href="/wiki/Method_acting" title="Method acting">method acting</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Lee_Strasberg_Theatre_and_Film_Institute" title="Lee Strasberg Theatre and Film Institute">Lee Strasberg Theatre and Film Institute</a> for ten years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leestrasburgalumna_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-leestrasburgalumna-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-instylestrasberg_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-instylestrasberg-24">[24]</a></sup> After high school, her mother encouraged her to apply for the <a href="/wiki/Collaborative_Arts_Project_21_(CAP21)" title="Collaborative Arts Project 21 (CAP21)">Collaborative Arts Project 21 (CAP21)</a>, a musical theater training <a href="/wiki/Music_school" title="Music school">conservatory</a> at <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">New York University</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Tisch_School_of_the_Arts" title="Tisch School of the Arts">Tisch School of the Arts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jmgaga_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-jmgaga-11">[11]</a></sup> One of 20 students to gain early admission, she, aged 17, lived in an <a href="/wiki/New_York_University_residence_halls" title="New York University residence halls">NYU dorm</a> on 11th Street.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-growingupgaga_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-growingupgaga-21">[21]</a></sup> In addition to sharpening her songwriting skills, she composed essays and analytical papers on art, religion, social issues, and politics, including a thesis on pop artists <a href="/wiki/Spencer_Tunick" title="Spencer Tunick">Spencer Tunick</a> and <a href="/wiki/Damien_Hirst" title="Damien Hirst">Damien Hirst</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-always-famous_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-always-famous-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARTISTdirect_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-ARTISTdirect-26">[26]</a></sup> She also auditioned for various roles and won the part of an unsuspecting diner customer for MTV's <i><a href="/wiki/Boiling_Points" title="Boiling Points">Boiling Points</a></i>, a prank reality television show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jmgaga_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-jmgaga-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2005.E2.80.932007:_Career_beginnings">2005–2007: Career beginnings</span></h3>
<p>At age 19, Gaga withdrew from CAP21 in the second semester of her sophomore year, deciding to focus on her musical career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv_55_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtv_55-28">[28]</a></sup> In mid-2005, Gaga recorded a couple of songs with hip-hop singer <a href="/wiki/Melle_Mel" title="Melle Mel">Grandmaster Melle Mel</a>, for an audio book accompanying Cricket Casey's children's book <i>The Portal in the Park</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jmgaga_11-4"><a href="#cite_note-jmgaga-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> She also formed a band called the Stefani Germanotta Band (SGBand) with some friends from NYU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jmgaga_11-5"><a href="#cite_note-jmgaga-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-growingupgaga_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-growingupgaga-21">[21]</a></sup> The band played at gigs around New York becoming a local fixture of the downtown Lower East Side club scene.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-growingupgaga_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-growingupgaga-21">[21]</a></sup> After the 2006 <a href="/wiki/Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame" title="Songwriters Hall of Fame">Songwriters Hall of Fame</a> New Songwriters Showcase at <a href="/wiki/The_Cutting_Room" title="The Cutting Room">The Cutting Room</a> in June, Gaga was recommended to music producer <a href="/wiki/Rob_Fusari" title="Rob Fusari">Rob Fusari</a> by talent scout Wendy Starland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fusari1_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fusari1-30">[30]</a></sup> Fusari collaborated with Gaga, who traveled daily to New Jersey, to work on songs she had written and to compose new material with him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jmgaga_11-6"><a href="#cite_note-jmgaga-11">[11]</a></sup> According to the producer, they began dating in May 2006, and he claimed to have created the "Lady Gaga" moniker after the <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a> song "<a href="/wiki/Radio_Ga_Ga" title="Radio Ga Ga">Radio Ga Ga</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fusari2_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fusari2-31">[31]</a></sup> The singer was in the process of trying to come up with a stage name when she received a text message from Fusari that read "Lady Gaga". He explained, "Every day, when Stef came to the studio, instead of saying hello, I would start singing 'Radio Ga Ga'". The text message was the result of a <a href="/wiki/T9_(predictive_text)" title="T9 (predictive text)">predictive text</a> glitch that changed "radio" to "lady". Fusari said she texted back, "That's it", and declared, "Don't ever call me Stefani again."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nj.com_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nj.com-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Contactmusic.com_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Contactmusic.com-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fusari and Gaga established a company called Team Lovechild LLC to promote her career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fusari2_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fusari2-31">[31]</a></sup> They recorded and produced <a href="/wiki/Electropop" title="Electropop">electropop</a> tracks and sent them to music industry executives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Joshua Sarubin, the head of <a href="/wiki/Artists_and_repertoire" title="Artists and repertoire">A&amp;R</a> at <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam Recordings</a>, responded positively and after agreement from his boss, <a href="/wiki/L.A._Reid" title="L.A. Reid">Antonio "L.A." Reid</a>, Gaga was signed to Def Jam in September 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jmgaga_11-7"><a href="#cite_note-jmgaga-11">[11]</a></sup> However, she was dropped by the label after only three months – a period of her life that later inspired the music video of her 2011 single "<a href="/wiki/Marry_the_Night" title="Marry the Night">Marry the Night</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allmusic_bio_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusic_bio-35">[35]</a></sup> Devastated, Gaga returned to the solace of the family home for Christmas and the nightlife culture of the Lower East Side. She became increasingly experimental: fascinating herself with emerging <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-burlesque" title="Neo-burlesque">neo-burlesque</a> shows, <a href="/wiki/Go-go_dancing" title="Go-go dancing">go-go dancing</a> at bars dressed in little more than a bikini, in addition to experimenting with drugs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Gaga explained her antics represented freedom: "I went to a Catholic school but it was on the New York underground that I found myself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jmgaga_11-8"><a href="#cite_note-jmgaga-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Times_Online.co.uk_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Times_Online.co.uk-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-always-famous_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-always-famous-25">[25]</a></sup> Her relationship with Fusari ended in January 2007 following which she became romantically involved with a <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a> drummer. She compared this relationship and the subsequent breakup to the musical film <i><a href="/wiki/Grease_(film)" title="Grease (film)">Grease</a></i>: "I was his Sandy, and he was my Danny, and I just broke."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsannual_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsannual-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_at_Lollapalooza_2007.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="798" data-file-width="1280" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Lady_Gaga_at_Lollapalooza_2007.jpg/220px-Lady_Gaga_at_Lollapalooza_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Lady_Gaga_at_Lollapalooza_2007.jpg/330px-Lady_Gaga_at_Lollapalooza_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Lady_Gaga_at_Lollapalooza_2007.jpg/440px-Lady_Gaga_at_Lollapalooza_2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_at_Lollapalooza_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gaga (right) performing with <a href="/wiki/Lady_Starlight" title="Lady Starlight">Lady Starlight</a> at <a href="/wiki/Lollapalooza" title="Lollapalooza">Lollapalooza</a> 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During this time, she met performance artist <a href="/wiki/Lady_Starlight" title="Lady Starlight">Lady Starlight</a>, who helped mold her onstage persona.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blast_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Blast-38">[38]</a></sup> Like SGBand, the pair soon began performing at many of the downtown club venues like the <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Lounge" title="Mercury Lounge">Mercury Lounge</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Bitter_End" title="The Bitter End">The Bitter End</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Rockwood_Music_Hall" title="Rockwood Music Hall">Rockwood Music Hall</a>. Their live performance art piece was known as "Lady Gaga and the Starlight Revue" and, billed as "The Ultimate Pop Burlesque Rockshow", was a low-fi tribute to 1970s variety acts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seattleweekly_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-seattleweekly-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Their performance at the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Lollapalooza" title="Lollapalooza">Lollapalooza</a> music festival<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMagazine_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-WMagazine-41">[41]</a></sup> was critically acclaimed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seattleweekly_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-seattleweekly-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>Having initially focused on <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">avant-garde</a> <a href="/wiki/Electronic_dance_music" title="Electronic dance music">electronic dance music</a>, Gaga found her musical <a href="/wiki/Niche_market" title="Niche market">niche</a> when she began to incorporate pop melodies and the <a href="/wiki/Glam_rock" title="Glam rock">glam rock</a> of <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a> and Queen into her music. While Gaga and Starlight were busy performing, Fusari continued to work on the songs he had created with Gaga. He sent these songs to his friend, producer and <a href="/wiki/Music_executive" title="Music executive">record executive</a> <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Herbert" title="Vincent Herbert">Vincent Herbert</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trans26_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-trans26-42">[42]</a></sup> The latter was quick to sign her to his label Streamline Records, an <a href="/wiki/Trade_name" title="Trade name">imprint</a> of <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>, established in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newimprent_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-newimprent-43">[43]</a></sup> Gaga later credited Herbert as the man who discovered her, adding: "I really feel like we made pop history, and we're gonna keep going."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trans26_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-trans26-42">[42]</a></sup> Having served as an apprentice songwriter during an internship at <a href="/wiki/Famous_Music" title="Famous Music">Famous Music Publishing</a>, (later acquired by <a href="/wiki/Sony/ATV_Music_Publishing" title="Sony/ATV Music Publishing">Sony/ATV Music Publishing</a>), Gaga subsequently struck a <a href="/wiki/Music_publisher_(popular_music)" title="Music publisher (popular music)">music publishing</a> deal with Sony/ATV. As a result, she was hired to write songs for <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a> and label mates <a href="/wiki/New_Kids_on_the_Block" title="New Kids on the Block">New Kids on the Block</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fergie_(singer)" title="Fergie (singer)">Fergie</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Pussycat_Dolls" title="The Pussycat Dolls">The Pussycat Dolls</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcover_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbcover-44">[44]</a></sup> At Interscope, singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Akon" title="Akon">Akon</a> recognized her vocal abilities when she sang a reference vocal for one of his tracks in studio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-totallygaga_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-totallygaga-45">[45]</a></sup> Akon then convinced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interscope_Geffen_A%26M" title="Interscope Geffen A&amp;M">Interscope Geffen A&amp;M</a> Chairman and CEO <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Iovine" title="Jimmy Iovine">Jimmy Iovine</a> to form a joint deal by having her also sign with his own label <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kon_Live_Distribution" title="Kon Live Distribution">Kon Live</a>, making her his "franchise player".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allmusic_bio_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusic_bio-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-franchise_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-franchise-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>Towards the end of 2007, Gaga met with songwriter and producer <a href="/wiki/RedOne" title="RedOne">RedOne</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hitquarters.com_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-hitquarters.com-47">[47]</a></sup> Gaga collaborated with him in the recording studio for a week on her debut album, and also joined the roster of <a href="/wiki/Cherrytree_Records" title="Cherrytree Records">Cherrytree Records</a>, an Interscope imprint established by producer and songwriter <a href="/wiki/Martin_Kierszenbaum" title="Martin Kierszenbaum">Martin Kierszenbaum</a>; she also wrote four songs with Kierszenbaum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcover_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbcover-44">[44]</a></sup> Despite her secure record deal, she admitted that there was fear about her being too "racy", "dance-oriented" and "underground" for the mainstream market. Her response: "My name is Lady Gaga, I've been on the music scene for years, and I'm telling you, this is what's next."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-independent-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2008.E2.80.932010:_The_Fame_and_The_Fame_Monster">2008–2010: <i>The Fame</i> and <i>The Fame Monster</i></span></h3>
<p>By 2008, Gaga relocated to Los Angeles in order to work extensively with her record label to complete her debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fame" title="The Fame">The Fame</a></i>, and set up her own creative team called the <a href="/wiki/Haus_of_Gaga" title="Haus of Gaga">Haus of Gaga</a>, modeled on <a href="/wiki/Andy_Warhol" title="Andy Warhol">Andy Warhol</a>'s <a href="/wiki/The_Factory" title="The Factory">Factory</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Contactmusic.com_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-Contactmusic.com-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ehqueenofpop_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-ehqueenofpop-48">[48]</a></sup> <i>The Fame</i> was released on August 19, 2008, with positive reception. Critics noted the album's combination of genres, "from <a href="/wiki/Def_Leppard" title="Def Leppard">Def Leppard</a> drums and hand claps to metal drums on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_music" title="Urban music">urban tracks</a>", the inspiration drawn from 1980s <a href="/wiki/Synthpop" title="Synthpop">synthpop</a> and incorporation of dance music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allmusic_bio_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusic_bio-35">[35]</a></sup> <i>The Fame</i> went to number one in Austria, Canada, Germany, Ireland, Switzerland and the UK and appeared in the top five in Australia, the US and 15 other countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Its first two singles, "<a href="/wiki/Just_Dance_(song)" title="Just Dance (song)">Just Dance</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Poker_Face_(Lady_Gaga_song)" title="Poker Face (Lady Gaga song)">Poker Face</a>", became worldwide commercial successes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smashhits_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-smashhits-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Poker_Face_on_acharts_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Poker_Face_on_acharts-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lady_Gaga_World_Tour_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lady_Gaga_World_Tour-53">[53]</a></sup> "Poker Face" won the award for Best Dance Recording at the <a href="/wiki/52nd_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="52nd Annual Grammy Awards">52nd Annual Grammy Awards</a> while <i>The Fame</i> won <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Dance/Electronica_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Dance/Electronica Album">Best Dance/Electronica Album</a> at the same ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Three other successful singles were released from the album—"<a href="/wiki/Eh,_Eh_(Nothing_Else_I_Can_Say)" title="Eh, Eh (Nothing Else I Can Say)">Eh, Eh (Nothing Else I Can Say)</a>", "<a href="/wiki/LoveGame" title="LoveGame">LoveGame</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Paparazzi_(Lady_Gaga_song)" title="Paparazzi (Lady Gaga song)">Paparazzi</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Poker_Face_on_acharts_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-Poker_Face_on_acharts-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Monster_Ball_-_Poker_Face_revamped2-tweak.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="491" data-file-width="416" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/The_Monster_Ball_-_Poker_Face_revamped2-tweak.jpg/220px-The_Monster_Ball_-_Poker_Face_revamped2-tweak.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/The_Monster_Ball_-_Poker_Face_revamped2-tweak.jpg/330px-The_Monster_Ball_-_Poker_Face_revamped2-tweak.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b4/The_Monster_Ball_-_Poker_Face_revamped2-tweak.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Monster_Ball_-_Poker_Face_revamped2-tweak.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gaga performing on The Monster Ball Tour in 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following her opening act on <a href="/wiki/The_Pussycat_Dolls" title="The Pussycat Dolls">The Pussycat Dolls</a>' 2009 <a href="/wiki/Doll_Domination_Tour" title="Doll Domination Tour">Doll Domination Tour</a> in Europe and Oceania, Gaga embarked on her own worldwide <a href="/wiki/The_Fame_Ball_Tour" title="The Fame Ball Tour">The Fame Ball Tour</a>, which ran from March to September 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> While she traveled the globe, Gaga released <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fame_Monster" title="The Fame Monster">The Fame Monster</a></i>, an EP of eight songs, in November 2009. Each song dealt with the darker side of fame from personal experience, expressed through a <a href="/wiki/Paranoia" title="Paranoia">monster</a> metaphor. Lead single "<a href="/wiki/Bad_Romance" title="Bad Romance">Bad Romance</a>" topped the charts in 18 countries and reached number two in the US, Australia and New Zealand; it won the Grammy Award for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Female_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Female Pop Vocal Performance">Best Female Pop Vocal Performance</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Short_Form_Music_Video" title="Grammy Award for Best Short Form Music Video">Best Short Form Music Video</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Two other singles were released from the EP, "<a href="/wiki/Telephone_(song)" title="Telephone (song)">Telephone</a>" (featuring <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>) and "<a href="/wiki/Alejandro_(song)" title="Alejandro (song)">Alejandro</a>". The former became Gaga's fourth UK number one single, while the latter faced controversy for its music video, which was deemed <a href="/wiki/Blasphemy" title="Blasphemy">blasphemous</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_League_(U.S.)" title="Catholic League (U.S.)">Catholic League</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Despite the controversy surrounding her music videos, Gaga became the first artist to gain over one billion <a href="/wiki/Viral_video" title="Viral video">viral views</a> on video-sharing website <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2010_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2010 MTV Video Music Awards">2010 MTV Video Music Awards</a>, Gaga won 8 of her 13 nominations, including <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Video_of_the_Year" title="MTV Video Music Award for Video of the Year">Video of the Year</a> for "Bad Romance".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> As a result, she became the most nominated artist and the first female to receive two nominations for Video of the Year at a single ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> In addition, <i>The Fame Monster</i> won the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Pop_Vocal_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Pop Vocal Album">Grammy Award for Best Pop Vocal Album</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Gaga also released, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Remix_(Lady_Gaga_album)" title="The Remix (Lady Gaga album)">The Remix</a></i>, which became her final record with Cherrytree Records.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> With worldwide sales of 500,000, it remains <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_remix_albums" title="List of best-selling remix albums">among the best-selling remix albums of all time</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> first listed Gaga on their 2010 <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Celebrity_100" title="Forbes Celebrity 100">Celebrity 100</a> and <a href="/wiki/Forbes_list_of_The_World%27s_100_Most_Powerful_Women" title="Forbes list of The World's 100 Most Powerful Women">World's Most Powerful Women</a> lists ranking her fourth and seventh, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>The success of <i>The Fame</i> and <i>The Fame Monster</i> allowed Gaga to start her second worldwide concert tour, <a href="/wiki/The_Monster_Ball_Tour" title="The Monster Ball Tour">The Monster Ball Tour</a>, just weeks after finishing The Fame Ball Tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbannounceball_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbannounceball-70">[70]</a></sup> Critically and commercially successful, the tour began in November 2009 and ended in May 2011, and grossed $227.4 million, making it the highest-grossing for a debut headlining artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Concerts performed at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a> in New York City were filmed for an <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> television special titled <i><a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga_Presents_the_Monster_Ball_Tour:_At_Madison_Square_Garden" title="Lady Gaga Presents the Monster Ball Tour: At Madison Square Garden">Lady Gaga Presents the Monster Ball Tour: At Madison Square Garden</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Gaga also performed songs from the albums at international events such as the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Royal_Variety_Performance" title="Royal Variety Performance">Royal Variety Performance</a>, <a href="/wiki/52nd_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="52nd Annual Grammy Awards">52nd Annual Grammy Awards</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_BRIT_Awards" title="2010 BRIT Awards">2010 BRIT Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Other performances might have included her participation in <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>'s <a href="/wiki/This_Is_It_(concerts)" title="This Is It (concerts)">This Is It</a> concert series at London's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_O2_Arena_(London)" title="The O2 Arena (London)">O<sub>2</sub> Arena</a> had he not died of a drug overdose. Gaga clarified that she was: "actually asked to open for Michael on his tour... We were going to open for him at the O<sub>2</sub> and we were working on making it happen. I believe there was some talk about us, lots of the openers, doing duets with Michael on stage."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>During this era Gaga ventured into business, collaborating with consumer electronics company <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monster_Cable_Products" title="Monster Cable Products">Monster Cable Products</a> to create a pair of in-ear, jewel-encrusted, headphones titled Heartbeats. "They are designed to be the first ever fashion accessories that double as the absolute best sonically sounding headphones in the world," she commented.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Gaga also partnered with <a href="/wiki/Polaroid_Corporation" title="Polaroid Corporation">Polaroid</a> in January 2010 as their Creative Director and revealed a trio of new photo capturing products called Grey Label.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> But her collaboration with past producer, and ex-boyfriend, Rob Fusari led to her production team, Mermaid Music LLC, being sued in March 2010 when he claimed that he was entitled to a 20% share of the company's earnings. The <a href="/wiki/New_York_Supreme_Court" title="New York Supreme Court">New York Supreme Court</a> dismissed both the lawsuit and a countersuit by Gaga.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> In addition to such strife, Gaga was tested borderline positive for <a href="/wiki/Systemic_lupus_erythematosus" title="Systemic lupus erythematosus">lupus</a>, but claimed not to be affected by the symptoms. The singer addressed the matter in an interview with <a href="/wiki/Larry_King" title="Larry King">Larry King</a>, saying she hopes to avoid symptoms by maintaining a healthy lifestyle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-comeparty_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-comeparty-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011.E2.80.932014:_Born_This_Way.2C_Artpop_and_Cheek_to_Cheek">2011–2014: <i>Born This Way</i>, <i>Artpop</i> and <i>Cheek to Cheek</i></span></h3>
<p>In February 2011, Gaga released the lead single "<a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_(song)" title="Born This Way (song)">Born This Way</a>" from <a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_(album)" title="Born This Way (album)">her studio album of the same name</a>. The song debuted atop the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, becoming the 1,000th number-one single in the history of the charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Its second single "<a href="/wiki/Judas_(Lady_Gaga_song)" title="Judas (Lady Gaga song)">Judas</a>" also peaked within the top ten in several major musical markets, while "<a href="/wiki/The_Edge_of_Glory" title="The Edge of Glory">The Edge of Glory</a>", first a commercial success in digital outlets, was later released as a single to rave critical reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> <i>Born This Way</i>, released on May 23, 2011, debuted atop the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> with first-week sales of 1.108 million copies, and topped the charts in more than 20 other countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The album sold eight million copies worldwide, and received three Grammy Award nominations, including her third Album of the Year listing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> The album's following singles "<a href="/wiki/You_and_I_(Lady_Gaga_song)" title="You and I (Lady Gaga song)">You and I</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Marry_the_Night" title="Marry the Night">Marry the Night</a>" failed to match the international success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-youandimv_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-youandimv-89">[89]</a></sup> In July 2011, she started dating actor and model <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Kinney" title="Taylor Kinney">Taylor Kinney</a>, whom she met while filming the "You and I" music video.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The accompanying tour for <i>Born This Way</i>, titled the <a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_Ball" title="Born This Way Ball">Born This Way Ball</a>, began in April 2012 and concluded in February 2013. Some of the tour's shows were cancelled due to a <a href="/wiki/Acetabular_labrum" title="Acetabular labrum">labral</a> tear of her right hip.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Shortly thereafter Gaga confirmed that she had hip surgery, and was recovering.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The tour earned $186.82 million globally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Gaga was ranked as the second most-played artist of 2011 in the United Kingdom by the <a href="/wiki/Phonographic_Performance_Limited" title="Phonographic Performance Limited">PPL</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> She also topped the Celebrity 100 List, with earnings of $90 million, and was the highest ranked entertainer on <i>Forbes</i> World's Most Powerful Women in the eleventh position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> In March 2012, Gaga was ranked fourth on <i>Billboard</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s list of top moneymakers of 2011 with earnings of $25 million, which included sales from <i>Born This Way</i> and her Monster Ball Tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>During this period, Gaga recorded a jazz version of "<a href="/wiki/The_Lady_Is_a_Tramp" title="The Lady Is a Tramp">The Lady Is a Tramp</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Tony_Bennett" title="Tony Bennett">Tony Bennett</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> and lent her vocals to a song with <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a> for the animated feature film, <i><a href="/wiki/Gnomeo_%26_Juliet" title="Gnomeo &amp; Juliet">Gnomeo &amp; Juliet</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> She held a concert at the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Town_Hall" title="Sydney Town Hall">Sydney Town Hall</a>, Australia, to promote <i>Born This Way</i>, and at the celebration of former US president <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>'s 65th birthday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Later that year, Gaga directed the critically acclaimed Thanksgiving Day television special, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Very_Gaga_Thanksgiving" title="A Very Gaga Thanksgiving">A Very Gaga Thanksgiving</a></i>, which attained 5.749 million American viewers, and spawned the release of her fourth EP, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Very_Gaga_Holiday" title="A Very Gaga Holiday">A Very Gaga Holiday</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> In May 2012, Gaga guest-starred as an animated version of herself on the 23rd-season finale of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></i>, titled "<a href="/wiki/Lisa_Goes_Gaga" title="Lisa Goes Gaga">Lisa Goes Gaga</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> She also appeared in Tony Bennett's documentary film, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Zen_of_Bennett" title="The Zen of Bennett">The Zen of Bennett</a></i> (2012).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> The following month, she announced her first fragrance in association with <a href="/wiki/Coty,_Inc." title="Coty, Inc.">Coty, Inc.</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga_Fame" title="Lady Gaga Fame">Lady Gaga Fame</a></i>, which was released worldwide in September 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pressrelease_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-pressrelease-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_ArtRave_San_Diego_(14702414241)_cropped.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2167" data-file-width="1690" height="282" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Lady_Gaga_ArtRave_San_Diego_%2814702414241%29_cropped.jpg/220px-Lady_Gaga_ArtRave_San_Diego_%2814702414241%29_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Lady_Gaga_ArtRave_San_Diego_%2814702414241%29_cropped.jpg/330px-Lady_Gaga_ArtRave_San_Diego_%2814702414241%29_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Lady_Gaga_ArtRave_San_Diego_%2814702414241%29_cropped.jpg/440px-Lady_Gaga_ArtRave_San_Diego_%2814702414241%29_cropped.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_ArtRave_San_Diego_(14702414241)_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gaga promoting <i>Artpop</i> with the <a href="/wiki/ArtRave:_The_Artpop_Ball" title="ArtRave: The Artpop Ball">ArtRave: The Artpop Ball</a> tour, 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>New songs for Gaga's third studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Artpop" title="Artpop">Artpop</a></i>, were beginning to take definite form as she worked with producer <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Garibay" title="Fernando Garibay">Fernando Garibay</a> in early 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Work on the album continued well into the Born This Way Ball tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> She yearned to make audiences have "a really good time" with <i>Artpop</i>, crafting the album to mirror "a night at the club".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv222_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtv222-114">[114]</a></sup> <i>Artpop</i> was released in November 2013. Despite mixed reviews,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> it debuted atop the <i>Billboard</i> 200 chart, and has sold 2.5 million copies as of July 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> The album spawned successful singles in "<a href="/wiki/Applause_(Lady_Gaga_song)" title="Applause (Lady Gaga song)">Applause</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Do_What_U_Want" title="Do What U Want">Do What U Want</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> singer <a href="/wiki/R._Kelly" title="R. Kelly">R. Kelly</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dowhatSingleAnnouncement_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-dowhatSingleAnnouncement-120">[120]</a></sup> A third release, "<a href="/wiki/G.U.Y." title="G.U.Y.">G.U.Y.</a>", became Gaga's weakest performing single to date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-radioit_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-radioit-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Gaga embarked on the accompanying <a href="/wiki/ArtRave:_The_Artpop_Ball" title="ArtRave: The Artpop Ball">ArtRave: The Artpop Ball</a> tour several months later, building upon concepts from her <a href="/wiki/ArtRave" title="ArtRave">ArtRave</a> promotional event. Scooping up $83 million, the itinerary saw her visit new cities and several locations initially included in the Born This Way Ball tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pr1_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-pr1-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Meanwhile, Gaga split from longtime manager Troy Carter over "creative differences",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NY_news_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-NY_news-125">[125]</a></sup> and by June 2014, she and new manager Bobby Campbell joined Artist Nation, the artist management division of <a href="/wiki/Live_Nation_Entertainment" title="Live Nation Entertainment">Live Nation Entertainment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tourforce_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-tourforce-126">[126]</a></sup> She topped <i>Forbes</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span> List of Top-Earning Celebs Under 30, and ranked second on the Celebrity 100 List and <a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)"><i>Time</i></a><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> anniversary poll of the most influential people of the past ten years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fusetv_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fusetv-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gaga starred in <a href="/wiki/Robert_Rodriguez" title="Robert Rodriguez">Robert Rodriguez</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Machete_Kills" title="Machete Kills">Machete Kills</a></i> (2013), a critical and commercial failure that earned her a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Raspberry_Award_for_Worst_Supporting_Actress" title="Golden Raspberry Award for Worst Supporting Actress">Golden Raspberry Award for Worst Supporting Actress</a> nomination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> The singer also hosted the November 16, 2013 episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i>, where she performed "Do What U Want" (with Kelly) and an album cut, "<a href="/wiki/Gypsy_(Lady_Gaga_song)" title="Gypsy (Lady Gaga song)">Gypsy</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nov2013SNL_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nov2013SNL-131">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-snlarchives_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-snlarchives-132">[132]</a></sup> Later that month, she held her second Thanksgiving Day television special on <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga_and_the_Muppets_Holiday_Spectacular" title="Lady Gaga and the Muppets Holiday Spectacular">Lady Gaga and the Muppets Holiday Spectacular</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thanksgiving2013_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thanksgiving2013-133">[133]</a></sup> Gaga had a cameo in another Robert Rodriguez film, <i><a href="/wiki/Sin_City:_A_Dame_to_Kill_For" title="Sin City: A Dame to Kill For">Sin City: A Dame to Kill For</a></i>, released on August 22, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GagaNailedIt_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-GagaNailedIt-134">[134]</a></sup> She was confirmed as the <a href="/wiki/Versace" title="Versace">Versace</a>'s spring-summer 2014 face with a campaign called "Lady Gaga For Versace".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, Gaga collaborated with American jazz singer Tony Bennett on the jazz album <i><a href="/wiki/Cheek_to_Cheek_(album)" title="Cheek to Cheek (album)">Cheek to Cheek</a></i>. She explained her inspiration behind the album: "<i>Cheek to Cheek</i> came out of a very organic friendship and relationship that Tony and I have built over the years and it truly was a collaborative effort... I've been singing jazz since I was a child and really wanted to show the authentic side of the genre."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-press_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-press-137">[137]</a></sup> The album received generally favorable reviews,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mc_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-mc-138">[138]</a></sup> with Caroline Sullivan of <i>The Guardian</i> praising Gaga's vocals in it, and <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Tribune" title="Chicago Tribune">Chicago Tribune</a></i> critic Howard Reich wrote that "<i>Cheek to Cheek</i> serves up the real thing, start to finish".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guarrev_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-guarrev-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> The album debuted atop the <i>Billboard</i> 200, becoming Gaga's third consecutive number-one record in the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usc2c_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-usc2c-141">[141]</a></sup> and went on to win a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Traditional_Pop_Vocal_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Traditional Pop Vocal Album">Grammy Award for Best Traditional Pop Vocal Album</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> The duo recorded a concert special, called <i><a href="/wiki/Tony_Bennett_and_Lady_Gaga:_Cheek_to_Cheek_Live!" title="Tony Bennett and Lady Gaga: Cheek to Cheek Live!">Tony Bennett and Lady Gaga: Cheek to Cheek Live!</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> and embarked on the <a href="/wiki/Cheek_to_Cheek_Tour" title="Cheek to Cheek Tour">Cheek to Cheek Tour</a>, which began in December 2014 and concluded in August 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> The same year, Gaga also had a <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga_Live_at_Roseland_Ballroom" title="Lady Gaga Live at Roseland Ballroom">seven-day residency show</a> commemorating the final performance at New York's <a href="/wiki/Roseland_Ballroom" title="Roseland Ballroom">Roseland Ballroom</a> before its closure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RS_Lady_Gaga_to_close_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-RS_Lady_Gaga_to_close-145">[145]</a></sup> She also released her second fragrance in association with Coty Inc., named <a href="/wiki/Eau_de_Gaga" title="Eau de Gaga">Eau de Gaga</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015.E2.80.93present:_American_Horror_Story_and_Joanne">2015–present: <i>American Horror Story</i> and <i>Joanne</i></span></h3>
<p>Gaga began 2015 with her engagement to Taylor Kinney in February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> Later that month, she performed at the <a href="/wiki/87th_Academy_Awards" title="87th Academy Awards">87th Academy Awards</a>, where she sang a medley of songs from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sound_of_Music_(film)" title="The Sound of Music (film)">The Sound of Music</a></i> in a cut-glass English accent. The performance triggered over 214,000 interactions per minute globally on <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> Gaga then performed a piano version of <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Imagine_(John_Lennon_song)" title="Imagine (John Lennon song)">Imagine</a>" at the opening ceremony of the <a href="/wiki/2015_European_Games" title="2015 European Games">2015 European Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a>, Azerbaijan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> She and <a href="/wiki/Diane_Warren" title="Diane Warren">Diane Warren</a> co-wrote the song "<a href="/wiki/Til_It_Happens_to_You" title="Til It Happens to You">Til It Happens to You</a>" for the documentary <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hunting_Ground" title="The Hunting Ground">The Hunting Ground</a></i>, which earned them the <a href="/wiki/Satellite_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Satellite Award for Best Original Song">Satellite Award for Best Original Song</a> and an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> nomination in <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">the same category</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> A few months later, Gaga and Tony Bennett featured in a commercial for <a href="/wiki/Barnes_%26_Noble" title="Barnes &amp; Noble">Barnes &amp; Noble</a>'s 2015 holiday campaign, for which they recorded a rendition of "<a href="/wiki/Baby,_It%27s_Cold_Outside" title="Baby, It's Cold Outside">Baby, It's Cold Outside</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BarnesNoble_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-BarnesNoble-152">[152]</a></sup> Outside of music, Gaga appeared in <a href="/wiki/Nick_Knight_(photographer)" title="Nick Knight (photographer)">Nick Knight</a>'s 2015 fashion film for <a href="/wiki/Tom_Ford" title="Tom Ford">Tom Ford</a>'s 2016 spring campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> From October 2015 to January 2016, she starred as a hotel owner named Elizabeth in the fifth season of the horror show <i><a href="/wiki/American_Horror_Story" title="American Horror Story">American Horror Story</a></i>, entitled <i><a href="/wiki/American_Horror_Story:_Hotel" title="American Horror Story: Hotel">Hotel</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seasonbegin_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-seasonbegin-154">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> Gaga's performance received mixed reviews,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> though she won a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actress_%E2%80%93_Miniseries_or_Television_Film" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actress – Miniseries or Television Film">Golden Globe Award for Best Actress – Miniseries or Television Film</a> for her role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> She followed with signing with the <a href="/wiki/Creative_Artists_Agency" title="Creative Artists Agency">Creative Artists Agency</a> (CAA) having previously been signed with <a href="/wiki/William_Morris_Endeavor" title="William Morris Endeavor">William Morris Endeavor</a> (WME).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_Super_Bowl_50_National_anthem.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2075" data-file-width="1633" height="280" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Lady_Gaga_Super_Bowl_50_National_anthem.jpg/220px-Lady_Gaga_Super_Bowl_50_National_anthem.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Lady_Gaga_Super_Bowl_50_National_anthem.jpg/330px-Lady_Gaga_Super_Bowl_50_National_anthem.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Lady_Gaga_Super_Bowl_50_National_anthem.jpg/440px-Lady_Gaga_Super_Bowl_50_National_anthem.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_Super_Bowl_50_National_anthem.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gaga after singing the National Anthem at the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_50" title="Super Bowl 50">Super Bowl 50</a> in February 2016</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For Gaga, 2015 ended with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Award_for_Woman_of_the_Year" title="Billboard Music Award for Woman of the Year">Woman of the Year</a> award from <i>Billboard</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2015bbwoman_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-2015bbwoman-159">[159]</a></sup> Among other accolades, she received Contemporary Icon Award at the 2015 Annual <a href="/wiki/Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame" title="Songwriters Hall of Fame">Songwriters Hall of Fame</a> Awards,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iconaward_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-iconaward-160">[160]</a></sup> and the Young Artist Award at the 2015 <a href="/wiki/National_Arts_Awards" title="National Arts Awards">National Arts Awards</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-artawards_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-artawards-161">[161]</a></sup> and ranked number 25 as the third female singer on the 2015 <i>Forbes</i> Celebrity 100 list, with earnings of $59 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> In January 2016, Gaga was invited to be the guest editor for the <i><a href="/wiki/V_(American_magazine)" title="V (American magazine)">V</a></i> magazine for its 99th issue, which features sixteen different covers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-V_mag_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-V_mag-163">[163]</a></sup> She subsequently received the award for Editor of the Year for her work on the magazine in March during the Fashion Los Angeles Awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gaga performed live at several places in 2016. These included singing the <a href="/wiki/The_Star-Spangled_Banner" title="The Star-Spangled Banner">US national anthem</a> in February, at <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_50" title="Super Bowl 50">Super Bowl 50</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> partnering with <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a> and Nile Rodgers for a tribute performance to the late <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a> at the <a href="/wiki/58th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="58th Annual Grammy Awards">58th Annual Grammy Awards</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> and singing "Til It Happens to You" at the <a href="/wiki/88th_Academy_Awards" title="88th Academy Awards">88th Academy Awards</a>, where she was introduced by <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a> and accompanied on-stage by 50 sexual assault survivors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> Gaga, in April 2016, was honored at the Jane Ortner Education Award by <a href="/wiki/The_Grammy_Museum" title="The Grammy Museum">The Grammy Museum</a>, with the Jane Ortner Artist Award, which recognizes artists who has demonstrated passion and dedication to education through the arts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gardner_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gardner-169">[169]</a></sup> To suppot their charities, Gaga and Elton John released a clothing and accessories line at <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy's">Macy's</a> in May 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lovebravery_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-lovebravery-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gaga played a witch named Scathach in <i><a href="/wiki/American_Horror_Story:_Roanoke" title="American Horror Story: Roanoke">American Horror Story: Roanoke</a></i>, the series' sixth iteration,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> which ran from September to November 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> Her role in the fifth season of the show ultimately influenced the creative process of her fifth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Joanne_(album)" title="Joanne (album)">Joanne</a></i>. She told <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i>, "[I] returned to something I've believed in so much, which is the art of darkness".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> She released the album's lead single "<a href="/wiki/Perfect_Illusion" title="Perfect Illusion">Perfect Illusion</a>" in September 2016,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> which debuted at number one in France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> <i>Joanne</i> was released the following month, and sold 170,000 copies in the US during its first week, becoming Gaga's fourth album to reach number one in the nation. As a result, Gaga became the first woman to have four US number one albums in the 2010s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> To promote <i>Joanne</i>, Gaga embarked on a three-date tour, sponsored by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bud_Light" title="Bud Light">Bud Light</a>, called <a href="/wiki/Dive_Bar_Tour" title="Dive Bar Tour">Dive Bar Tour</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> The album's second single "<a href="/wiki/Million_Reasons" title="Million Reasons">Million Reasons</a>" was released later, which she performed at the <a href="/wiki/Victoria%27s_Secret_Fashion_Show_2016" title="Victoria's Secret Fashion Show 2016">Victoria's Secret Fashion Show 2016</a> in Paris.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Upcoming_projects">Upcoming projects</span></h4>
<p>Gaga's future projects include starring in <a href="/wiki/Bradley_Cooper" title="Bradley Cooper">Bradley Cooper</a>'s remake of the 1954 <a href="/wiki/Musical_film" title="Musical film">musical drama film</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Star_Is_Born_(1954_film)" title="A Star Is Born (1954 film)">A Star Is Born</a></i>, as well as creating new music for the project. Filming is scheduled to commence in 2017,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> and the film is expected to be released on September 28, 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> Gaga will also perform at the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LI_halftime_show" title="Super Bowl LI halftime show">Super Bowl LI halftime show</a> on February 5, 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry">Artistry</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style">Musical style</span></h3>
<p>Continually experimenting with new musical ideas and images, Gaga's musical and performance style is the subject of much analysis and scrutiny from critics. She professes that she is "liberating" herself by constantly reinventing her sound and image, insisting that she has been drawn to such a practice since her childhood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> Refusing to <a href="/wiki/Lip_sync" title="Lip sync">lip sync</a>, Gaga – whose range is frequently compared to those of Madonna and <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stefani" title="Gwen Stefani">Gwen Stefani</a> – has manipulated her vocal style over the course of her career yet considers <i>Born This Way</i> (2011) "much more vocally up to par with what I've always been capable of."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> In summation of her voice, <i>Entertainment Weekly</i> wrote: "There's an immense emotional intelligence behind the way she uses her voice. Almost never does she overwhelm a song with her vocal ability, recognizing instead that artistry is to be found in nuance rather than lung power."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> Gaga possesses a <a href="/wiki/Mezzo-soprano" title="Mezzo-soprano">mezzo-soprano</a> vocal range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although her early lyrics have been criticized for lacking intellectual stimulation, "[Gaga] does manage to get you moving and grooving at an almost effortless pace."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popmatters_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-popmatters-189">[189]</a></sup> Gaga believes that "all good music can be played on a piano and still sound like a hit."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> She has covered a wide variety of topics in her songs: while <i>The Fame</i> (2008) meditates on the lust for stardom, <i>The Fame Monster</i> (2009) expresses fame's dark side through monster metaphors. <i>Born This Way</i> (2011) is sung in English, French, German, and Spanish and includes common themes in Gaga's controversial songwriting such as: sex, love, religion, money, drugs, identity, liberation, sexuality, freedom, and individualism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-albumguide_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-albumguide-191">[191]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-btwrs_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-btwrs-192">[192]</a></sup></p>
<p>Her music style has been described as <a href="/wiki/Electropop" title="Electropop">electropop</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> and as <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> and the structure of her music is said to be influenced by classic 1980s pop and 1990s <a href="/wiki/Europop" title="Europop">Europop</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BG_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-BG-195">[195]</a></sup> Her debut album <i>The Fame</i> (2008) provoked <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" title="The Sunday Times">The Sunday Times</a></i> to assert "in combining music, fashion, art and technology, [Gaga] evokes Madonna, Gwen Stefani circa '<a href="/wiki/Hollaback_Girl" title="Hollaback Girl">Hollaback Girl</a>', <a href="/wiki/Kylie_Minogue" title="Kylie Minogue">Kylie Minogue</a> 2001 or <a href="/wiki/Grace_Jones" title="Grace Jones">Grace Jones</a> right now", and a critic from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Globe" title="The Boston Globe">The Boston Globe</a></i> to comment that she draws: "obvious inspirations from Madonna to Gwen Stefani... in [her] girlish but sturdy pipes and bubbly beats."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> Music critic <a href="/wiki/Simon_Reynolds" title="Simon Reynolds">Simon Reynolds</a> wrote that: "Everything about Gaga came from <a href="/wiki/Electroclash" title="Electroclash">electroclash</a>, except the music, which wasn't particularly 1980s, just ruthlessly catchy naughties pop glazed with <a href="/wiki/Auto-Tune" title="Auto-Tune">Auto-Tune</a> and undergirded with <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a>-ish beats."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> The follow-up <i>The Fame Monster</i> (2009), saw Gaga's taste for pastiche, drawing on "Seventies arena glam, perky <a href="/wiki/ABBA" title="ABBA">ABBA</a> disco, and sugary throwbacks like <a href="/wiki/Stacey_Q" title="Stacey Q">Stacey Q</a>" while <i>Born This Way</i> (2011) also draws on the records of her childhood and still has the "electro-sleaze beats and Eurodisco chorus chants" of its predecessor but includes genres as diverse as opera, heavy metal, <a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-albumguide_191-1"><a href="#cite_note-albumguide-191">[191]</a></sup> "There isn't a subtle moment on the album, but even at its nuttiest, the music is full of wide-awake emotional details," wrote <i>Rolling Stone</i>, which concluded: "The more excessive Gaga gets, the more honest she sounds."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-btwrs_192-1"><a href="#cite_note-btwrs-192">[192]</a></sup> With 2014's <i>Cheek to Cheek</i>, Gaga dabbled in the <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a> genre. Although critically appreciated for her love of the music, and the songs she recorded on the album, it was noted that Gaga's attempt to switch genres, with "her rhythmically square, shouty delivery", left her vocals sounding more like a Broadway singer than a real jazz musician.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:290px;max-width:290px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:133px;max-width:133px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rebel_Heart_WTG_(3).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="579" data-file-width="405" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Rebel_Heart_WTG_%283%29.jpg/131px-Rebel_Heart_WTG_%283%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Rebel_Heart_WTG_%283%29.jpg/197px-Rebel_Heart_WTG_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Rebel_Heart_WTG_%283%29.jpg/262px-Rebel_Heart_WTG_%283%29.jpg 2x" width="131"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:153px;max-width:153px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:David_Bowie_(1987).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="945" data-file-width="761" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/David_Bowie_%281987%29.jpg/151px-David_Bowie_%281987%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/David_Bowie_%281987%29.jpg/227px-David_Bowie_%281987%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/David_Bowie_%281987%29.jpg/302px-David_Bowie_%281987%29.jpg 2x" width="151"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Music artists such as Madonna and David Bowie have influenced Gaga</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Gaga grew up listening to artists such as: <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder" title="Stevie Wonder">Stevie Wonder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Grateful_Dead" title="The Grateful Dead">The Grateful Dead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">Led Zeppelin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blondie_(band)" title="Blondie (band)">Blondie</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Garbage_(band)" title="Garbage (band)">Garbage</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> who all influenced her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-familyinfluence_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-familyinfluence-201">[201]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-She.27s_The_Greatest_Of_All_Time_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-She.27s_The_Greatest_Of_All_Time-202">[202]</a></sup> She has cited heavy metal bands as an influence, stating that <a href="/wiki/Iron_Maiden" title="Iron Maiden">Iron Maiden</a> "changed my life" and describing herself as "the biggest <a href="/wiki/Black_Sabbath" title="Black Sabbath">Black Sabbath</a> fan on Earth".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> Gaga's musical inspiration varies from <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a> singers like <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> to glam rock artists like <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury" title="Freddie Mercury">Freddie Mercury</a>, as well as the theatrics of the <a href="/wiki/Pop_art"
