title="Pop art">pop artist</a> <a href="/wiki/Andy_Warhol" title="Andy Warhol">Andy Warhol</a> and her own performance roots in musical theater.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allmusic_bio_35-3"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusic_bio-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-soundtrack_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-soundtrack-206">[206]</a></sup> Gaga has often been compared to Madonna who admits that she sees herself reflected in Gaga.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> In response to the comparisons, Gaga stated in February 2011: "I don't want to sound presumptuous, but I've made it my goal to revolutionize pop music. The last revolution was launched by Madonna 25 years ago" in addition to commenting that: "there is really no one that is a more adoring and loving Madonna fan than me."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> Like Madonna, Gaga has continued to reinvent herself and has drawn inspiration from the music and performances of a diverse mix of artists including: <a href="/wiki/Cyndi_Lauper" title="Cyndi Lauper">Cyndi Lauper</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Depeche_Mode" title="Depeche Mode">Depeche Mode</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gigwise_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gigwise-210">[210]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prince_(musician)" title="Prince (musician)">Prince</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-prince1_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-prince1-211">[211]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-prince_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-prince-212">[212]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lily_Allen" title="Lily Allen">Lily Allen</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marilyn_Manson" title="Marilyn Manson">Marilyn Manson</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yoko_Ono" title="Yoko Ono">Yoko Ono</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ace_of_Base" title="Ace of Base">Ace of Base</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amber_(singer)" title="Amber (singer)">Amber</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Grace_Jones" title="Grace Jones">Grace Jones</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> Beyoncé,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another spiritual influence on Gaga has been the Indian physician, public speaker, and writer <a href="/wiki/Deepak_Chopra" title="Deepak Chopra">Deepak Chopra</a>. Labeling him a "true inspiration", she stated that "he's always reminded me to work in a life of service to my fans and to fulfill my vision and my destiny" in addition to thinking about Chopra when it comes to her work as a musician: "I want so much for it to go beyond the music for my fans."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> Gaga also lifted a quote from <a href="/wiki/Rajneesh" title="Rajneesh">Osho</a>'s book <i>Creativity</i> on Twitter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LGOC35_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-LGOC35-222">[222]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> When asked about her connection to him, Gaga said she was influenced by his work and that, for her, "the creativity is the greatest way of rebellion": "Equality", she concluded, "is one of the most important things in my life."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gaga has identified fashion as a major influence and claimed that her interest in fashion came from her mother who was "always very well kept and beautiful."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timesonline2_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-timesonline2-225">[225]</a></sup> Her musical endeavors are directly linked with fashion with the singer explaining: "When I'm writing music, I'm thinking about the clothes I want to wear on stage. It's all about everything altogether—performance art, pop performance art, fashion."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv_55_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-mtv_55-28">[28]</a></sup> Gaga has been stylistically compared to <a href="/wiki/Leigh_Bowery" title="Leigh Bowery">Leigh Bowery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isabella_Blow" title="Isabella Blow">Isabella Blow</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cher" title="Cher">Cher</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Times_Online.co.uk_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-Times_Online.co.uk-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv_55_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-mtv_55-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ourladyvogue_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-ourladyvogue-226">[226]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cherfashionsense_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-cherfashionsense-227">[227]</a></sup> She commented that as a child, she somehow absorbed Cher's out-there fashion sense and made it her own.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cherfashionsense_227-1"><a href="#cite_note-cherfashionsense-227">[227]</a></sup> Gaga considers <a href="/wiki/Donatella_Versace" title="Donatella Versace">Donatella Versace</a> her <a href="/wiki/Muse" title="Muse">muse</a>, and the late English fashion designer and close friend <a href="/wiki/Alexander_McQueen" title="Alexander McQueen">Alexander McQueen</a> as an inspiration, admitting that "I miss Lee every time I get dressed" while channeling him in some of her work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Times_Online.co.uk_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-Times_Online.co.uk-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-comeparty_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-comeparty-81">[81]</a></sup> In turn, Versace calls Lady Gaga "the fresh Donatella".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> Modeled on Andy Warhol's Factory, Gaga has her own creative production team, which she handles personally, called the Haus of Gaga, who create many of her clothes, stage props, and hairdos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> Other fashion influences came from <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana, Princess of Wales">Princess Diana</a>: "I love Princess Diana so much. She was an enormous influence on me when I was younger because my mother worshiped her so much. When she died, I'll never forget, my mother was crying. It was this very powerful moment in my childhood watching my mother so connected to someone".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Videos_and_stage">Videos and stage</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Monster_Ball_-_Alejandro_revamped2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/The_Monster_Ball_-_Alejandro_revamped2.jpg/220px-The_Monster_Ball_-_Alejandro_revamped2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/The_Monster_Ball_-_Alejandro_revamped2.jpg/330px-The_Monster_Ball_-_Alejandro_revamped2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/The_Monster_Ball_-_Alejandro_revamped2.jpg/440px-The_Monster_Ball_-_Alejandro_revamped2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Monster_Ball_-_Alejandro_revamped2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gaga during a "blood stained" performance in 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With constant costume changes and provocative visuals, Gaga's music videos are often described as short films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parvis_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-parvis-231">[231]</a></sup> "Being provocative is not just about getting people's attention. It's about saying something that really affects people in a real way, in a positive way," she professes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parvis_231-1"><a href="#cite_note-parvis-231">[231]</a></sup> According to author Curtis Fogel, exploring <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bondage_(sexual)" title="Bondage (sexual)">bondage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sadomasochism" title="Sadomasochism">sadomasochism</a> in addition to highlighting prevalent feminist themes, "the three central themes that shape Gaga's music videos are sex, violence, and power."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-criticaldebate_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-criticaldebate-232">[232]</a></sup> While she labels herself "a little bit of a feminist" and asserts that she is "sexually empowering women",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ultimatepredator_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-ultimatepredator-233">[233]</a></sup> Gaga strives to empower young women to stand up for what they believe in.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-criticaldebate_232-1"><a href="#cite_note-criticaldebate-232">[232]</a></sup> "She not only reiterates her assertion of total originality," professed pop critic <a href="/wiki/Ann_Powers" title="Ann Powers">Ann Powers</a>, "but also finesses it until it's both a philosophical stance about how constructing a persona from pop-cultural sources can be an expression of a person's truth—<a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%C3%A0_la" title="wikt:à la">a la</a> those drag queens Gaga sincerely admires—and a bit of a feminist act."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> In summation of her videos, <i>Rolling Stone</i> used the <a href="/wiki/Rhetoric" title="Rhetoric">rhetoric</a>: "does anyone look to a Lady Gaga video for restraint?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-youandimv_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-youandimv-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>Her performances are described as "highly entertaining and innovative"; the blood-spurting performance of "Paparazzi" at the <a href="/wiki/2009_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2009 MTV Video Music Awards">2009 MTV Video Music Awards</a> was described as "eye-popping" by MTV News.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> She continued the "blood soaked" theme during The Monster Ball Tour, and triggered protests in England from family groups and fans in the aftermath of a local tragedy, in which a taxi driver had murdered 12 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> Her unconventionality continued at the <a href="/wiki/2011_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2011 MTV Video Music Awards">2011 MTV Video Music Awards</a>: appearing in <a href="/wiki/Drag_(clothing)" title="Drag (clothing)">drag</a> as her male <a href="/wiki/Alter_ego" title="Alter ego">alter ego</a>, Jo Calderone, and delivering a lovesick monologue before a performance of her song "You and I".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> As Gaga's choreographer and creative director, <a href="/wiki/Laurieann_Gibson" title="Laurieann Gibson">Laurieann Gibson</a> provided material for her shows and videos for four years only to be replaced by Gibson's assistant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richard_%22Richy%22_Jackson_(choreographer)" title='Richard "Richy" Jackson (choreographer)'>Richard Jackson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-byebyegibson_238-0"><a href="#cite_note-byebyegibson-238">[238]</a></sup> Gaga admits to being a perfectionist when it comes to her elaborate shows. "I'm very bossy. I can scream my head off if I see one light fixture out. I'm very detailed – every minute of the show has got to be perfect."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parvis_231-2"><a href="#cite_note-parvis-231">[231]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_image">Public image</span></h2>
<p>Public reception of Gaga's music, fashion sense and persona are polarized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Molanphy_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-Molanphy-239">[239]</a></sup> Her status as a role model, self-esteem booster for her fans, trailblazer, and fashion icon who breathes new life into the industry is by turns affirmed and denied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> Critics have pointed out her unique place in pop music, the need for new movements in popular culture, the attention Gaga brings to modern social issues, and the inherently subjective nature of her art.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-influence3_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-influence3-243">[243]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> In view of her influence on modern culture and her rise to global fame, sociologist Mathieu Deflem of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Carolina" title="University of South Carolina">University of South Carolina</a> has offered a course titled "Lady Gaga and the Sociology of the Fame" since spring 2011 with the objective of unravelling: "some of the sociologically relevant dimensions of the fame of Lady Gaga."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup> When Gaga briefly met with US president <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> at a Human Rights Campaign fundraiser, he described the interaction as "intimidating" as she was dressed in 16-inch heels making her undoubtedly the tallest woman in the room.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_Americano_Manchester_cropped.jpg"><img alt="Gaga in a false meat dress with her dancers" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3030" data-file-width="2715" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Lady_Gaga_Americano_Manchester_cropped.jpg/220px-Lady_Gaga_Americano_Manchester_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Lady_Gaga_Americano_Manchester_cropped.jpg/330px-Lady_Gaga_Americano_Manchester_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Lady_Gaga_Americano_Manchester_cropped.jpg/440px-Lady_Gaga_Americano_Manchester_cropped.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_Americano_Manchester_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gaga performing in a pseudo meat dress, September 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Towards the end of 2008, comparisons were made between the fashions of Gaga and Aguilera, that noted similarities in their styling, hair, and make-up.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Times_Online.co.uk_14-4"><a href="#cite_note-Times_Online.co.uk-14">[14]</a></sup> Aguilera stated that she was "completely unaware of [Gaga]".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Times_Online.co.uk_14-5"><a href="#cite_note-Times_Online.co.uk-14">[14]</a></sup> Comparisons continued into 2010, when Aguilera released the music video of her single "<a href="/wiki/Not_Myself_Tonight" title="Not Myself Tonight">Not Myself Tonight</a>". Critics noted similarities between the song and its accompanying music video and Gaga's video for "Bad Romance".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> When interviewed by <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Walters" title="Barbara Walters">Barbara Walters</a> for her annual <a href="/wiki/ABC_News" title="ABC News">ABC News</a> special <i><a href="/wiki/Barbara_Walters%27_10_Most_Fascinating_People" title="Barbara Walters' 10 Most Fascinating People">10 Most Fascinating People</a></i> in 2009, Gaga dismissed the claim that she is <a href="/wiki/Intersex" title="Intersex">intersex</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Urban_legend" title="Urban legend">urban legend</a>. Responding to a question on this issue, she stated, "At first it was very strange and everyone sorta said, 'That's really quite a story!' But in a sense, I portray myself in a very <a href="/wiki/Androgyny" title="Androgyny">androgynous</a> way, and I love androgyny."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-walters_249-0"><a href="#cite_note-walters-249">[249]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gaga's outlandish fashion sense has also been one of her characteristic aspects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Global_Language_Monitor" title="Global Language Monitor">Global Language Monitor</a> named "Lady Gaga" as the Top Fashion Buzzword with her trademark "no pants" a close third.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> put her outfits on its end of the decade "best-of" list, saying: "Whether it's a dress made of Muppets or strategically placed bubbles, Gaga's <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/outr%C3%A9" title="wikt:outré">outré</a> ensembles brought performance art into the mainstream."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup> <i>Time</i> placed Gaga on their All-Time 100 Fashion Icons List amongst some of Gaga's inspirations such as Michael Jackson, Madonna, and The Beatles, stating: "Lady Gaga is just as notorious for her outrageous style as she is for her pop hits. After all, Gaga, born Stefani Germanotta, has sported outfits made from plastic bubbles, <a href="/wiki/Kermit_the_Frog" title="Kermit the Frog">Kermit the Frog</a> dolls, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meat_dress_of_Lady_Gaga" title="Meat dress of Lady Gaga">raw meat</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gaga wore a <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga%27s_meat_dress" title="Lady Gaga's meat dress">dress made of raw beef</a> to the <a href="/wiki/2010_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2010 MTV Video Music Awards">2010 MTV Video Music Awards</a> which was supplemented by boots, a purse, and a hat also made out of raw beef.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-254">[254]</a></sup> Partly awarded in recognition of the dress, <i><a href="/wiki/Vogue_(magazine)" title="Vogue (magazine)">Vogue</a></i> named her one of the Best Dressed people of 2010 while <i>Time</i> named the dress the Fashion Statement of 2010. However, it promted divided opinions, attracting the attention of worldwide media but also invoking the fury of animal rights organization <a href="/wiki/People_for_the_Ethical_Treatment_of_Animals" title="People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals">PETA</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup> In 2012, Gaga became a feature of a temporary exhibition <i>The Elevated: From the Pharaoh to Lady Gaga</i> marking the 150th anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum,_Warsaw" title="National Museum, Warsaw">National Museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-warsawvoice_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-warsawvoice-258">[258]</a></sup> Gaga was presented in a dress of raw meat, described by Polish weekly <i><a href="/wiki/Wprost" title="Wprost">Wprost</a></i> as: "an icon of modernity elevated by the power which she exercises over mass media".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wprost_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-wprost-259">[259]</a></sup> The meat dress was later displayed at the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Women_in_the_Arts" title="National Museum of Women in the Arts">National Museum of Women in the Arts</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup> and entered the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> in September 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup> As Gaga appeared at the 87th Academy Awards and subsequent events, she changed her style and fashion, transforming into a more glamorous person; <i>Vogue</i> compared her to that of <a href="/wiki/Marilyn_Monroe" title="Marilyn Monroe">Marilyn Monroe</a> and <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a> described the change as "more acceptably 'natural' or 'classic'".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup></p>
<p>While devout followers call Gaga "Mother Monster", Gaga often refers to her fans as "Little Monsters" which she had tattooed on herself in dedication.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-monsters_265-0"><a href="#cite_note-monsters-265">[265]</a></sup> To some, this <a href="/wiki/Dichotomy" title="Dichotomy">dichotomy</a> contravenes the concept of outsider culture. <a href="/wiki/Camille_Paglia" title="Camille Paglia">Camille Paglia</a>, in her 2010 cover story "Lady Gaga and the death of sex" in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" title="The Sunday Times">The Sunday Times</a></i>, asserts that Gaga: "is more an identity thief than an erotic taboo breaker, a mainstream manufactured product who claims to be singing for the freaks, the rebellious and the dispossessed when she is none of those."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> Writing for <i>The Guardian</i>, <a href="/wiki/Kitty_Empire" title="Kitty Empire">Kitty Empire</a> opined that the dichotomy: "...allows the viewer to have a 'transgressive' experience without being required to think. At [her performance's] core, though, is the idea that Gaga is at one with the freaks and outcasts."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_268-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-268">[268]</a></sup> In July 2012, Gaga also co-founded the website LittleMonsters.com, which became the first official <a href="/wiki/Social_networking_service" title="Social networking service">social network</a> devoted to <a href="/wiki/Stan_(fan)" title="Stan (fan)">fans</a> of an artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Activism">Activism</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LadyGaga-EqualityMarch-Crop.jpg"><img alt="A blond woman wearing a white shirt and black glasses speaking on a lectern carrying a 'National Equality March' poster. Behind her is a white stone balustrade of a building." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1820" data-file-width="1442" height="278" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/LadyGaga-EqualityMarch-Crop.jpg/220px-LadyGaga-EqualityMarch-Crop.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/LadyGaga-EqualityMarch-Crop.jpg/330px-LadyGaga-EqualityMarch-Crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/LadyGaga-EqualityMarch-Crop.jpg/440px-LadyGaga-EqualityMarch-Crop.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LadyGaga-EqualityMarch-Crop.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gaga delivering a speech at the 2009 <a href="/wiki/National_Equality_March" title="National Equality March">National Equality March</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Alongside her music career, Gaga has contributed to various charities. For natural disasters, Gaga has helped various relief efforts. Although declining an invitation to appear on the single "<a href="/wiki/We_Are_the_World_25_for_Haiti" title="We Are the World 25 for Haiti">We Are the World 25</a>" to benefit victims of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">2010 Haiti earthquake</a>, she donated the proceeds of her concert of January 24, 2010, at New York's <a href="/wiki/Radio_City_Music_Hall" title="Radio City Music Hall">Radio City Music Hall</a> to the country's reconstruction relief fund.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup> All profits from her official online store on that day were also donated. Gaga announced that an estimated total of $500,000 was collected for the fund.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup> Hours after the <a href="/wiki/2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2011 Tōhoku earthquake and tsunami">2011 Tōhoku earthquake and tsunami</a> hit Japan on March 11, 2011, Gaga <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">tweeted</a> a message and a link to Japan Prayer Bracelets. All revenue from a bracelet she designed in conjunction with the company was donated to relief efforts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> As of March 29, 2011, the bracelets raised $1.5 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup> However, attorney Alyson Oliver filed a lawsuit against Gaga in Detroit in June 2011, noting that the bracelet was subject to a sales tax and an extra $3.99 shipping charge was added to the price. She also believed that not all proceeds from the bracelets would go to the relief efforts, demanding a public accounting of the campaign and refunds for people who had bought the bracelet. Gaga's spokesperson called the lawsuit "meritless" and "misleading".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbc-gaga-bracelet-lawsuit_274-0"><a href="#cite_note-msnbc-gaga-bracelet-lawsuit-274">[274]</a></sup> On June 25, 2011, Gaga performed at <a href="/wiki/MTV_Japan" title="MTV Japan">MTV Japan</a>'s charity show in <a href="/wiki/Makuhari_Messe" title="Makuhari Messe">Makuhari Messe</a>, which benefited the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Red_Cross" title="Japanese Red Cross">Japanese Red Cross</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, Gaga joined the anti-fracking campaign <a href="/wiki/Artists_Against_Fracking" title="Artists Against Fracking">Artists Against Fracking</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup> In October 2012, Gaga was reported to have met the founder of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikileaks" title="Wikileaks">Wikileaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julian_Assange" title="Julian Assange">Julian Assange</a>, at the Ecuadorean embassy in London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup> On October 9, 2012, <a href="/wiki/Yoko_Ono" title="Yoko Ono">Yoko Ono</a> gave Gaga and four other activists the <a href="/wiki/LennonOno_Grant_for_Peace" title="LennonOno Grant for Peace">LennonOno Grant for Peace</a> in <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk" title="Reykjavík">Reykjavík</a>, Iceland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup> On November 6, 2012, Gaga pledged to donate $1 million to the American Red Cross to help the victims of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandy" title="Hurricane Sandy">Hurricane Sandy</a>. Gaga also contributes in the fight against <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV and AIDS</a>, focusing on educating young women about the risks of the disease. In collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Cyndi_Lauper" title="Cyndi Lauper">Cyndi Lauper</a>, Gaga joined forces with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Make-up_Art_Cosmetics" title="Make-up Art Cosmetics">MAC Cosmetics</a> to launch a line of lipstick under their supplementary cosmetic line, Viva Glam. In a press release, Gaga declared, "I don't want Viva Glam to be just a lipstick you buy to help a cause. I want it to be a reminder when you go out at night to put a condom in your purse right next to your lipstick."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup> The sales of Gaga-endorsed Viva Glam lipstick and lip gloss have raised more than $202 million to fight HIV and AIDS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forbesprofile_280-0"><a href="#cite_note-forbesprofile-280">[280]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 7, 2016, Gaga joined <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">Vice President</a> Joe Biden at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Nevada,_Las_Vegas" title="University of Nevada, Las Vegas">University of Nevada, Las Vegas</a>, to support Biden's <a href="/wiki/White_House_Task_Force_to_Protect_Students_from_Sexual_Assault" title="White House Task Force to Protect Students from Sexual Assault">It's On Us</a> campaign as he travels to colleges on behalf of the organization, which has seen 250,000 students from more than 530 colleges sign a pledge of solidarity and activation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup> On June 26, 2016, Gaga attended the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Conference_of_Mayors" title="United States Conference of Mayors">84th Annual US Conference of Mayors</a> in Indianapolis where she joined with <a href="/wiki/14th_Dalai_Lama" title="14th Dalai Lama">Dalai Lama</a> to talk about the power of kindness and how to make the world a more compassionate place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_government" title="Chinese government">Chinese government</a> added Gaga to a list of hostile foreign forces, and Chinese websites and media organizations were ordered to stop uploading or distributing her songs. The <a href="/wiki/Publicity_Department_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Publicity Department of the Communist Party of China">Publicity Department of the Communist Party of China</a> (CCPPD) also issued order for State-controlled media to condemn this meeting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283"><a href="#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup> On July 28, 2016, Gaga headlined a private concert in <a href="/wiki/Camden,_New_Jersey" title="Camden, New Jersey">Camden, New Jersey</a>, called Camden Rising, as part of the <a href="/wiki/2016_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2016 Democratic National Convention">2016 Democratic National Convention</a> in support of <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Born_This_Way_Foundation">Born This Way Foundation</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_Foundation" title="Born This Way Foundation">Born This Way Foundation</a></div>
<p>In 2012, she launched the <a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_Foundation" title="Born This Way Foundation">Born This Way Foundation</a> (BTWF), a non-profit organization that focuses on youth empowerment and issues like self-confidence, well-being, anti-bullying, mentoring, and career development. It takes its name from the 2011 single and album. The foundation plans to work with a number of partners, including the <a href="/wiki/John_D._and_Catherine_T._MacArthur_Foundation" title="John D. and Catherine T. MacArthur Foundation">John D. and Catherine T. MacArthur Foundation</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_California_Endowment" title="The California Endowment">The California Endowment</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berkman_Center_for_Internet_%26_Society" title="Berkman Center for Internet &amp; Society">Berkman Center for Internet &amp; Society</a> at Harvard University.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup> Media proprietor <a href="/wiki/Oprah_Winfrey" title="Oprah Winfrey">Oprah Winfrey</a>, writer <a href="/wiki/Deepak_Chopra" title="Deepak Chopra">Deepak Chopra</a>, and United States Secretary of Health and Human Services <a href="/wiki/Kathleen_Sebelius" title="Kathleen Sebelius">Kathleen Sebelius</a> spoke at the inauguration at <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[286]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup> The foundation's original funding included $1.2 million from Gaga, $500,000 from the MacArthur Foundation, and $850,000 from <a href="/wiki/Barneys_New_York" title="Barneys New York">Barneys New York</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[288]</a></sup> The foundation works in partnership with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berkman_Center_for_Internet_%26_Society" title="Berkman Center for Internet &amp; Society">Berkman Center for Internet &amp; Society</a> at Harvard University, the <a href="/wiki/John_D._and_Catherine_T._MacArthur_Foundation" title="John D. and Catherine T. MacArthur Foundation">MacArthur Foundation</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/California_Endowment" title="California Endowment">California Endowment</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289">[289]</a></sup> and, as lead media partner, <a href="/wiki/Viacom" title="Viacom">Viacom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup> In July 2012, the BTWF partnered with <a href="/wiki/Office_Depot" title="Office Depot">Office Depot</a>, which will donate 25% of the sales-a minimum of $1million-of a series of limited edition back-to-school products that promote the foundation's message<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup> The foundation's initiatives have included, in March–April 2012, a poster competition that asked participants to submit images that answer the question "What does bravery mean to you?";<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup> the "Born Brave Bus" that would follow her on tour as a youth drop-in center as an initiative against bullying,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup> and the "Born Brave" community and school groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup></p>
<p>On October 24, 2015, at the Yale Center for Emotional Intelligence, Gaga joined 200 high school students, top policy makers, and academic officials, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yale" title="Yale">Yale</a> President <a href="/wiki/Peter_Salovey" title="Peter Salovey">Peter Salovey</a>, a pioneer in the study of <a href="/wiki/Emotional_intelligence" title="Emotional intelligence">emotional intelligence</a>, to discuss ways to recognize and channel emotions for positive outcomes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296"><a href="#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup> In 2016, the foundation partnered with <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vox_Media" title="Vox Media">Vox Media</a> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Re/code" title="Re/code">Re/code</a></i> to fight online harassment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297"><a href="#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup> It was also announced that the sale of the cover of the 99th issue of the <a href="/wiki/V_(American_magazine)" title="V (American magazine)"><i>V</i> magazine</a>, which featured Gaga and Kinney, was donated to the foundation to bring cutting-edge, social-emotional intelligence research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-V_mag_163-1"><a href="#cite_note-V_mag-163">[163]</a></sup> Gaga and Elton John released a clothing and accessories line on <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy's">Macy's</a> on May 9, 2016, entitled Love Bravery, in which twenty-five percent of each purchase will support the Born This Way Foundation and the <a href="/wiki/Elton_John_AIDS_Foundation" title="Elton John AIDS Foundation">Elton John AIDS Foundation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lovebravery_170-1"><a href="#cite_note-lovebravery-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LGBT_advocacy">LGBT advocacy</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_DADT.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="726" data-file-width="1023" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Lady_Gaga_DADT.jpg/220px-Lady_Gaga_DADT.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Lady_Gaga_DADT.jpg/330px-Lady_Gaga_DADT.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Lady_Gaga_DADT.jpg/440px-Lady_Gaga_DADT.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga_DADT.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gaga speaking against "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_ask,_don%27t_tell" title="Don't ask, don't tell">Don't ask, don't tell</a>", in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Maine" title="Portland, Maine">Portland, Maine</a>, 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Gaga is an outspoken activist for <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_by_country_or_territory" title="LGBT rights by country or territory">LGBT rights worldwide</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-activist_298-0"><a href="#cite_note-activist-298">[298]</a></sup> She attributes much of her early success as a mainstream artist to her <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">gay</a> fans and is considered a gay icon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fabmag_299-0"><a href="#cite_note-fabmag-299">[299]</a></sup> Early in her career she had difficulty getting <a href="/wiki/Airplay" title="Airplay">radio airplay</a>, and stated, "The turning point for me was the gay community."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvgayicon_300-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtvgayicon-300">[300]</a></sup> She thanked FlyLife, a Manhattan-based <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> marketing company with whom her label Interscope works, in the liner notes of <i>The Fame</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thefame_301-0"><a href="#cite_note-thefame-301">[301]</a></sup> One of her first televised performances was in May 2008 at the <a href="/wiki/NewNowNext_Awards" title="NewNowNext Awards">NewNowNext Awards</a>, an awards show aired by the LGBT television network <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Logo_(TV_channel)" title="Logo (TV channel)">Logo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newnownext_302-0"><a href="#cite_note-newnownext-302">[302]</a></sup> In June of the same year, she performed at the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Pride" title="San Francisco Pride">San Francisco Pride</a> event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfpride_303-0"><a href="#cite_note-sfpride-303">[303]</a></sup> After <i>The Fame</i> was released, she revealed that the song "Poker Face" was about her <a href="/wiki/Bisexuality" title="Bisexuality">bisexuality</a>. In an interview with <i>Rolling Stone</i>, she spoke about how her boyfriends tended to react to her bisexuality, saying: "The fact that I'm into women, they're all intimidated by it. It makes them uncomfortable. They're like, 'I don't need to have a threesome. I'm happy with just you'."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsannual_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-rsannual-37">[37]</a></sup> When she appeared as a guest on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ellen_DeGeneres_Show" title="The Ellen DeGeneres Show">The Ellen DeGeneres Show</a></i> in May 2009, she praised DeGeneres for being: "an inspiration for women and for the gay community".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gaga spoke at the 2009 <a href="/wiki/National_Equality_March" title="National Equality March">National Equality March</a> in Washington, D.C. in support of LGBT movement, and described the appearance as "the single most important moment" of her career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup> She attended the <a href="/wiki/2010_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2010 MTV Video Music Awards">2010 MTV Video Music Awards</a> accompanied by four gay and lesbian former members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">United States Armed Forces</a> who had been unable to serve <a href="/wiki/Coming_out" title="Coming out">openly</a> under the U.S. military's "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_ask,_don%27t_tell" title="Don't ask, don't tell">Don't ask, don't tell</a>" (DADT) policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-306"><a href="#cite_note-306">[306]</a></sup> Gaga released three videos on YouTube urging her fans to contact their Senators in an effort to overturn DADT. In September 2010 she spoke at a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Servicemembers_Legal_Defense_Network" title="Servicemembers Legal Defense Network">Servicemembers Legal Defense Network</a>'s rally in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Maine" title="Portland, Maine">Portland, Maine</a>. Following this event, editors of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Advocate" title="The Advocate">The Advocate</a></i> commented that she had become a "fierce advocate" for gays and lesbians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307">[307]</a></sup> Gaga appeared at <a href="/wiki/Europride" title="Europride">Europride</a>, a pan-European international event dedicated to LGBT pride, held in Rome in June 2011. She criticized the intolerant state of <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Europe" title="LGBT rights in Europe">gay rights in many European countries</a> and described gay people as "revolutionaries of love".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvrome_308-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtvrome-308">[308]</a></sup> Gaga was ordained as a minister by the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Life_Church_Monastery" title="Universal Life Church Monastery">Universal Life Church Monastery</a> so that she could officiate the wedding of long-time friends, both of whom were women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309">[309]</a></sup> In June 2016, during a vigil held in Los Angeles for victims of the <a href="/wiki/2016_Orlando_nightclub_shooting" title="2016 Orlando nightclub shooting">attack at the gay nightclub Pulse</a> in Orlando, Gaga read aloud the names of the 49 people killed in the attack, and also gave a supporting speech.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310"><a href="#cite_note-310">[310]</a></sup> Also in June 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Campaign" title="Human Rights Campaign">Human Rights Campaign</a> released a video in tribute to the victims of that attack; in the video, Gaga and others told the stories of the people killed there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311">[311]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312"><a href="#cite_note-312">[312]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga,_ARTPOP_Ball_Tour,_Bell_Center,_Montr%C3%A9al,_2_July_2014_(60)_(14376655959).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Lady_Gaga%2C_ARTPOP_Ball_Tour%2C_Bell_Center%2C_Montr%C3%A9al%2C_2_July_2014_%2860%29_%2814376655959%29.jpg/220px-Lady_Gaga%2C_ARTPOP_Ball_Tour%2C_Bell_Center%2C_Montr%C3%A9al%2C_2_July_2014_%2860%29_%2814376655959%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Lady_Gaga%2C_ARTPOP_Ball_Tour%2C_Bell_Center%2C_Montr%C3%A9al%2C_2_July_2014_%2860%29_%2814376655959%29.jpg/330px-Lady_Gaga%2C_ARTPOP_Ball_Tour%2C_Bell_Center%2C_Montr%C3%A9al%2C_2_July_2014_%2860%29_%2814376655959%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Lady_Gaga%2C_ARTPOP_Ball_Tour%2C_Bell_Center%2C_Montr%C3%A9al%2C_2_July_2014_%2860%29_%2814376655959%29.jpg/440px-Lady_Gaga%2C_ARTPOP_Ball_Tour%2C_Bell_Center%2C_Montr%C3%A9al%2C_2_July_2014_%2860%29_%2814376655959%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lady_Gaga,_ARTPOP_Ball_Tour,_Bell_Center,_Montr%C3%A9al,_2_July_2014_(60)_(14376655959).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Global_Language_Monitor" title="Global Language Monitor">Global Language Monitor</a> named "Lady Gaga" as the Top Fashion Buzzword with her trademark "no pants".</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Gaga has been regarded as a trailblazer throughout several points in her career, sometimes utilizing controversy to bring attention to various issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313">[313]</a></sup> With the meteoric success of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fame" title="The Fame">The Fame</a></i>, Gaga is credited as being one of the frontrunners of the rise in the popularity of <a href="/wiki/Synthpop" title="Synthpop">synthpop</a> in the late 2000s and early 2010s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-314"><a href="#cite_note-314">[314]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315">[315]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup> "It's all about how you cultivate your community," writer <a href="/wiki/Brian_Solis" title="Brian Solis">Brian Solis</a> said. "Celebs have never shied away from causes and in many ways it's expected that they will use their celebrity to gain attention for those causes. But it's what (Gaga) does over time and how her community responds that starts the lean-over into the influence factor." <a href="/wiki/Polaroid_Corporation" title="Polaroid Corporation">Polaroid</a> CEO, after working with Gaga, said: "she's a true artist who inspires her fans and the creative community. The relationship she has with her fans is exceptionally close and she is consistently in contact with them via social networks, making her messages accessible, authentic and far reaching."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317"><a href="#cite_note-317">[317]</a></sup> Named the "Queen of Pop" in a ranking by <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine in 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Molanphy_239-1"><a href="#cite_note-Molanphy-239">[239]</a></sup> her work has influenced <a href="/wiki/Miley_Cyrus" title="Miley Cyrus">Miley Cyrus</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318">[318]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319">[319]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ellie_Goulding" title="Ellie Goulding">Ellie Goulding</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320"><a href="#cite_note-320">[320]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Halsey_(singer)" title="Halsey (singer)">Halsey</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-322"><a href="#cite_note-322">[322]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nick_Jonas" title="Nick Jonas">Nick Jonas</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-323"><a href="#cite_note-323">[323]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lorde" title="Lorde">Lorde</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-324"><a href="#cite_note-324">[324]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sam_Smith_(singer)" title="Sam Smith (singer)">Sam Smith</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325"><a href="#cite_note-325">[325]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Greyson_Chance" title="Greyson Chance">Greyson Chance</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326"><a href="#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Debbie_Harry" title="Debbie Harry">Debbie Harry</a> of <a href="/wiki/Blondie_(band)" title="Blondie (band)">Blondie</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dharry_327-0"><a href="#cite_note-dharry-327">[327]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Noah_Cyrus" title="Noah Cyrus">Noah Cyrus</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328"><a href="#cite_note-328">[328]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Tisdale" title="Ashley Tisdale">Ashley Tisdale</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-329"><a href="#cite_note-329">[329]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/MGMT" title="MGMT">MGMT</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-330"><a href="#cite_note-330">[330]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gaga has been commemorated in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scientific_name" title="Scientific name">scientific names</a> of several organisms. A new genus of <a href="/wiki/Fern" title="Fern">ferns</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Gaga_(genus)" title="Gaga (genus)">Gaga</a></i>, and two species, <i>G. germanotta</i> and <i>G. monstraparva</i> have been named in her honor. The name <i>monstraparva</i> alluded to Gaga's fans known as "little monsters" since their symbol is the outstretched "monster claw" hand, which resembles a tightly in-rolled young fern leaf prior to unfurling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-331"><a href="#cite_note-331">[331]</a></sup> Gaga also has an extinct mammal, <i><a href="/wiki/Gagadon" title="Gagadon">Gagadon</a> minimonstrum</i>, and a parasitic wasp, <i><a href="/wiki/Aleiodes_gaga" title="Aleiodes gaga">Aleiodes gaga</a></i>, named for her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stuck.26Covert2014_332-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stuck.26Covert2014-332">[332]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-333"><a href="#cite_note-333">[333]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Butcheretal2012_334-0"><a href="#cite_note-Butcheretal2012-334">[334]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Achievements">Achievements</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Lady_Gaga" title="List of awards and nominations received by Lady Gaga">List of awards and nominations received by Lady Gaga</a></div>
<p>As of January 2016, Gaga had sold an estimated 27 million albums and 146 million singles worldwide; her singles are some of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_singles" title="List of best-selling singles">best-selling worldwide</a>, making her one of <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">the best-selling music artists</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-335"><a href="#cite_note-335">[335]</a></sup> She is also noted as a touring force as she has grossed more than $300 million in revenue from 3.2 million tickets for her first three worldwide concert tours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tourforce_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-tourforce-126">[126]</a></sup> Her other achievements include six <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a>, three <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brit Awards</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-336"><a href="#cite_note-336">[336]</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe Award</a>, thirteen <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award" title="MTV Video Music Award">MTV Video Music Awards</a>, twelve <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame" title="Songwriters Hall of Fame">Songwriters Hall of Fame</a>'s Contemporary Icon Award, which she was the first artist ever to win,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iconaward_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-iconaward-160">[160]</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/National_Arts_Awards" title="National Arts Awards">National Arts Awards</a>' Young Artist Award, which honors individuals who have achieved incredible accomplishments and exemplary leadership while still early in their career,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-artawards_161-1"><a href="#cite_note-artawards-161">[161]</a></sup> and honored at the Jane Ortner Education Award by <a href="/wiki/The_Grammy_Museum" title="The Grammy Museum">The Grammy Museum</a>, with the Jane Ortner Artist Award, which recognizes artists who has demonstrated passion and dedication to education through the arts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gardner_169-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gardner-169">[169]</a></sup> She has also been recognized by the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Fashion_Designers_of_America" title="Council of Fashion Designers of America">Council of Fashion Designers of America</a> (CFDA) with the Fashion Icon lifetime achievement award, a special prize reserved for: "an individual whose style has made a significant impact on popular culture on an international stage".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-337"><a href="#cite_note-337">[337]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gaga has consecutively appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> magazine's Artists of the Year (scoring the definitive title in 2010),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-338"><a href="#cite_note-338">[338]</a></sup> and named as <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Women_in_Music" title="Billboard Women in Music">Woman of the Year</a> in 2015,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2015bbwoman_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-2015bbwoman-159">[159]</a></sup> is the fourth best selling digital singles artist in the United States according to <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">RIAA</a> with a total of 59 million certified.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-339"><a href="#cite_note-339">[339]</a></sup> She also became the first woman to receive the Digital Diamond Award from RIAA,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-340"><a href="#cite_note-340">[340]</a></sup> and is the first and only artist to have two songs pass 7 million downloads ("Poker Face" and "Just Dance").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-341"><a href="#cite_note-341">[341]</a></sup> She is regularly placed on lists composed by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forbesprofile_280-1"><a href="#cite_note-forbesprofile-280">[280]</a></sup> including their list of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forbes_Magazine%27s_List_of_The_World%27s_100_Most_Powerful_Women" title="Forbes Magazine's List of The World's 100 Most Powerful Women">The World's 100 Most Powerful Women</a> from 2010 to 2014,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-342"><a href="#cite_note-342">[342]</a></sup> named one of the most influential people in the world by <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine in 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-343"><a href="#cite_note-343">[343]</a></sup> and the "second most influential people of the past ten years" through a readers' poll in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fusetv_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fusetv-128">[128]</a></sup> In 2016 she was a finalist for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Advocate" title="The Advocate">The Advocate</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Person of the Year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-344"><a href="#cite_note-344">[344]</a></sup></p>
